## Agent 1: cognitive-science-learning-foundations

Based on my comprehensive search of the academic literature, I'll now provide structured findings on the foundational cognitive science of learning. Let me organize this information into a comprehensive landscape review.

# Foundational Cognitive Science of Learning: A Comprehensive Landscape (2018-2026)

## Executive Summary

This review synthesizes foundational cognitive science research on human learning and memory, with particular focus on applications in AI-enhanced education. The landscape spans seminal theories from cognitive psychology to cutting-edge AI applications in educational technology, covering memory encoding, cognitive load, desirable difficulties, transfer of learning, and attention/working memory constraints in digital environments.

## 1. Memory Encoding and Retrieval

### 1.1 Dual-Process Theories
Dual-process theories distinguish between two cognitive systems: System 1 (fast, automatic, intuitive) and System 2 (slow, deliberate, analytical). These theories have evolved to explain various memory phenomena including recognition, recall, and metacognitive judgments.

### 1.2 Levels of Processing Framework
The seminal work by **Craik and Lockhart (1972)** introduced the levels of processing framework, proposing that memory retention depends on the depth of cognitive processing during encoding. This framework has been refined over decades:

- **Craik and Tulving (1975)** demonstrated that semantic processing leads to better retention than shallow perceptual processing
- **Lockhart and Craik (1990)** provided a retrospective commentary on the framework's evolution
- **Craik (2002)** reviewed enduring legacies and addressed criticisms of the original formulation

### 1.3 Neural Basis of Memory
Recent neuroimaging research has identified key brain regions involved in memory processes:
- Prefrontal cortex for working memory and executive control
- Hippocampus for episodic memory formation
- Angular gyrus for semantic processing integration

## 2. Cognitive Load Theory and AI Optimization

### 2.1 Theoretical Foundations
Cognitive Load Theory (CLT), developed by **Sweller, van Merriënboer, and Paas**, posits that working memory has limited capacity and learning is optimized when instructional design minimizes extraneous load while managing intrinsic and germane loads.

### 2.2 Three Types of Cognitive Load
1. **Intrinsic Load**: Inherent difficulty of the material
2. **Extraneous Load**: Unnecessary cognitive processing imposed by instructional design
3. **Germane Load**: Cognitive resources devoted to schema construction and automation

### 2.3 AI Applications for Cognitive Load Optimization
Recent research demonstrates AI's potential for managing cognitive load:

**Kpogli et al. (2024)** proposed Cognitive Load–Adaptive Instructional Systems that integrate AI with learning sciences to reduce achievement gaps in K-12 education. Their framework systematically reduces extraneous cognitive load while improving learning equity across diverse student populations.

**Skulmowski and Xu (2021)** challenged traditional CLT assumptions in digital learning environments, arguing that some extraneous load in interactive media may actually enhance learning through increased engagement and deeper processing.

### 2.4 Measurement and Assessment
**Ouwehand et al. (2021)** investigated alternative methods for measuring cognitive load beyond traditional Likert scales, exploring more valid assessment techniques for educational research.

## 3. Desirable Difficulties and Learning Strategies

### 3.1 Theoretical Framework
The concept of "desirable difficulties" introduced by **Robert and Elizabeth Bjork** suggests that certain learning conditions that feel effortful and challenging actually enhance long-term retention and transfer.

### 3.2 Key Learning Strategies

#### 3.2.1 Spacing Effect
Distributed practice across time intervals significantly improves retention compared to massed practice. **Barzagar Nazari and Ebersbach (2018)** demonstrated the effectiveness of spacing in classroom settings with third and seventh graders.

#### 3.2.2 Interleaving
Mixing different types of problems or materials during practice enhances discrimination learning. **Birnbaum et al. (2012)** showed that interleaving improves inductive learning through enhanced discrimination and retrieval processes.

#### 3.2.3 Retrieval Practice
The testing effect demonstrates that actively retrieving information from memory strengthens learning more than passive restudy. **Tullis et al. (2012)** explored metacognitive awareness of the testing effect's benefits.

### 3.3 Implementation Challenges
**de Bruin et al. (2023)** introduced the Start and Stick to Desirable Difficulties (S2D2) Framework to address learners' resistance to engaging with effortful learning strategies despite their proven benefits.

## 4. Transfer of Learning

### 4.1 Near vs. Far Transfer
Transfer research distinguishes between near transfer (applying learning to similar contexts) and far transfer (applying learning to dissimilar contexts). Far transfer remains particularly challenging to achieve.

### 4.2 Analogical Reasoning
**Gick and Holyoak's** seminal work on analogical problem solving (1980, 1983) established that successful transfer often depends on recognizing structural similarities between problems rather than surface features.

### 4.3 Schema Induction
The ability to extract abstract principles from specific examples facilitates transfer to new situations. Research shows that multiple examples with varied surface features enhance schema induction.

## 5. Attention and Working Memory Constraints in Digital Learning

### 5.1 Working Memory Limitations
**Cowan (2001)** revised Miller's "magical number 7" to propose a more precise capacity limit of 3-5 chunks in working memory, with implications for instructional design.

### 5.2 Multimedia Learning Principles
Cognitive theory of multimedia learning integrates CLT with dual-channel (visual/auditory) processing assumptions to guide effective digital content design.

### 5.3 Digital Externalization Effects
**Skulmowski (2023)** reviewed cognitive offloading in digital environments, noting that while external storage reduces immediate cognitive load, it may negatively impact long-term learning by reducing encoding depth.

## 6. AI-Enhanced Education Applications (2018-2026)

### 6.1 Intelligent Tutoring Systems
Modern ITS integrate cognitive diagnostic models with machine learning and natural language processing to create adaptive learning environments. **Sarfaraj (2025)** reviewed conversational AI applications in intelligent tutoring.

### 6.2 Large Language Models in Education
**Yan et al. (2023)** conducted a systematic scoping review of practical and ethical challenges of LLMs in education, identifying key concerns around academic integrity, bias, and equitable access.

### 6.3 Adaptive Learning Systems
**Pesovski et al. (2024)** demonstrated generative AI applications for creating personalized learning materials, showing how AI can customize content based on individual learner needs and progress.

### 6.4 Learning Analytics
AI-powered analytics systems provide real-time insights into learning processes, enabling data-driven instructional decisions and personalized interventions.

### 6.5 Assessment and Evaluation
**Owan et al. (2023)** explored AI tools in educational measurement, highlighting applications in automated grading, personalized feedback generation, and adaptive testing.

## 7. Emerging Trends and Future Directions

### 7.1 Hybrid Intelligence
**Järvelä et al. (2025)** proposed human-AI coevolution models where AI systems and learners mutually adapt, creating synergistic learning environments that leverage both human creativity and AI computational power.

### 7.2 Cognitive-Affective-Social Integration
**Schneider et al. (2021)** introduced the Cognitive-Affective-Social Theory of Learning in digital Environments (CASTLE), emphasizing that social cues in digital materials activate social schemata and influence learning processes.

### 7.3 Immersive Learning Technologies
**Makransky and Petersen (2021)** developed the Cognitive Affective Model of Immersive Learning (CAMIL) to explain learning processes in virtual reality environments, considering both cognitive and affective factors.

### 7.4 Ethical Considerations
Growing concerns about AI's impact on critical thinking, cognitive engagement, and educational equity require careful consideration in system design and implementation.

## 8. Research Gaps and Opportunities

1. **Long-term Effects**: Limited research on long-term impacts of AI-enhanced learning on cognitive development
2. **Cross-cultural Validity**: Most research conducted in Western educational contexts
3. **Cognitive Load Measurement**: Need for more objective, real-time cognitive load assessment methods
4. **Transfer Enhancement**: Strategies to improve far transfer in AI-supported learning environments
5. **Teacher-AI Collaboration**: Optimal division of labor between human educators and AI systems

## 9. Methodological Considerations

### 9.1 Experimental Designs
Cognitive science research employs diverse methodologies including laboratory experiments, classroom interventions, neuroimaging studies, and computational modeling.

### 9.2 Measurement Approaches
Multiple measures of learning outcomes are essential, including retention tests, transfer tasks, and longitudinal assessments of knowledge application.

### 9.3 Ecological Validity
Balancing controlled experimental conditions with real-world educational contexts remains a persistent challenge in learning sciences research.

## 10. Practical Implications for Educational Design

### 10.1 Instructional Design Principles
1. Optimize cognitive load through careful content sequencing and presentation
2. Incorporate desirable difficulties through spaced, interleaved practice
3. Design for transfer using varied examples and explicit connections
4. Leverage multimedia principles for digital content design
5. Implement retrieval practice opportunities throughout learning sequences

### 10.2 AI System Design Guidelines
1. Maintain human oversight in AI-driven educational decisions
2. Ensure transparency in AI recommendations and feedback
3. Design for equitable access across diverse learner populations
4. Incorporate cognitive science principles in algorithm development
5. Support teacher professional development for AI integration

## Conclusion

The integration of cognitive science principles with AI technologies represents a transformative opportunity for education. By grounding AI-enhanced learning systems in empirically validated theories of human cognition, we can create more effective, engaging, and equitable educational experiences. Future research should focus on developing AI systems that not only adapt to learners' current knowledge states but also promote the development of robust, transferable knowledge structures and metacognitive skills essential for lifelong learning.

## Agent 2: adaptive-learning-systems-foundations

Based on my comprehensive search, I now have enough information to provide a structured research findings report. Let me compile the key papers and insights.

# Foundational Adaptive Learning Systems Research (2018-2026)

## Executive Summary

This research survey covers the comprehensive landscape of AI/ML applications in learning and studying, focusing on foundational adaptive learning systems. The analysis spans cognitive science of learning, adaptive learning systems, intelligent tutoring, learning analytics, LLMs in education, assessment & evaluation, self-regulated learning, and human-AI collaborative learning.

## 1. Adaptive Learning Platforms & Architecture

### Core Architecture Components
Adaptive learning platforms typically consist of:
- **Learner Modeling Engine**: Tracks student knowledge states and learning behaviors
- **Content Management System**: Organizes learning materials with metadata
- **Adaptation Engine**: Makes personalized recommendations based on learner models
- **Assessment Module**: Evaluates learning progress and mastery
- **Analytics Dashboard**: Provides insights for educators and learners

### Key Production Systems
While specific production platform papers were limited in the search results, the literature reveals several architectural patterns:
- **Microservices-based architectures** for scalability
- **Knowledge graph-based** content organization
- **Real-time adaptation engines** using streaming data processing
- **Multi-tenant architectures** for institutional deployment

## 2. Bayesian Knowledge Tracing (BKT) & Extensions

### Foundational BKT Models
**Bayesian Knowledge Tracing (BKT)** is a probabilistic model that estimates the probability a student has learned a skill based on their performance on related items. The standard BKT model includes four parameters:
- **p(L₀)**: Initial probability of knowing the skill
- **p(T)**: Probability of learning the skill after each opportunity
- **p(G)**: Probability of guessing correctly when not knowing
- **p(S)**: Probability of slipping (incorrect when knowing)

### Modern Extensions & Improvements

**Deonovic et al. (2018)** [Learning meets assessment](https://doi.org/10.1007/s41237-018-0070-z) establishes a fundamental connection between BKT and Item Response Theory (IRT), showing that the stationary distribution of BKT relates to IRT models. This paper bridges longitudinal (BKT) and cross-sectional (IRT) approaches to learner modeling.

**Bulut et al. (2023)** [An Introduction to Bayesian Knowledge Tracing with pyBKT](https://doi.org/10.3390/psych5030050) provides practical guidance on implementing BKT models using the pyBKT Python library, covering various BKT variants and their applications.

### Deep Learning Extensions
Recent research has extended BKT using deep learning approaches:
- **Deep Knowledge Tracing (DKT)**: Uses recurrent neural networks to model knowledge states
- **Dynamic Key-Value Memory Networks (DKVMN)**: Incorporates memory mechanisms for better knowledge representation
- **Attention-based models**: Improve interpretability and performance

## 3. Item Response Theory (IRT) in Digital Learning

### Core IRT Models
IRT models learner ability and item characteristics through probabilistic relationships:

**1PL (Rasch Model)**:
- Models only item difficulty
- \(P(X_{ij} = 1|\theta_i, b_j) = \frac{1}{1 + e^{-(\theta_i - b_j)}}\)

**2PL Model**:
- Adds item discrimination parameter
- \(P(X_{ij} = 1|\theta_i, a_j, b_j) = \frac{1}{1 + e^{-a_j(\theta_i - b_j)}}\)

**3PL Model**:
- Adds guessing parameter
- \(P(X_{ij} = 1|\theta_i, a_j, b_j, c_j) = c_j + (1-c_j)\frac{1}{1 + e^{-a_j(\theta_i - b_j)}}\)

### Applications in Adaptive Learning
IRT is used for:
- **Adaptive testing**: Selecting optimal items based on current ability estimates
- **Item banking**: Maintaining calibrated item pools
- **Vertical scaling**: Comparing performance across different tests
- **Differential item functioning**: Detecting item bias

## 4. Mastery-Based Progression & Competency Frameworks

### Mastery Learning Principles
Mastery-based systems ensure students demonstrate competency before progressing:
- **Clear learning objectives**: Specific, measurable competencies
- **Formative assessment**: Continuous feedback loops
- **Differentiated instruction**: Multiple pathways to mastery
- **Time flexibility**: Variable pacing based on individual needs

### Competency-Based Education (CBE) Frameworks
Modern CBE systems incorporate:
- **Micro-credentials**: Stackable, verifiable competencies
- **Learning pathways**: Personalized sequences based on prerequisite relationships
- **Portfolio assessment**: Evidence-based competency demonstration
- **Badging systems**: Digital recognition of achievements

### AI-Enhanced CBE Systems
**Huang (2025)** [Designing Human-AI Orchestrated Classrooms](https://doi.org/10.6914/aiese.010302) proposes AI-enabled scaling of CBE through diagnostic tracking, adaptive supply, and teacher orchestration pathways within a distributed cognition framework.

## 5. Learner Modeling & Knowledge State Estimation

### Knowledge Tracing Approaches
**Abdelrahman et al. (2022)** [Knowledge Tracing: A Survey](https://doi.org/10.1145/3569576) provides a comprehensive review of KT methods, covering:
- **Traditional approaches**: BKT, IRT, Performance Factors Analysis (PFA)
- **Deep learning methods**: DKT, DKVMN, Transformer-based models
- **Hybrid approaches**: Combining statistical and neural methods
- **Interpretable models**: Attention mechanisms, cognitive diagnosis models

### Prerequisite Knowledge Graphs
**Alzetta et al. (2023)** [Annotation Protocol for Textbook Enrichment with Prerequisite Knowledge Graph](https://doi.org/10.1007/s10758-023-09682-6) presents methods for extracting prerequisite relations from educational texts to build knowledge graphs that support adaptive learning path generation.

### Modern Learner Modeling Techniques
- **Graph Neural Networks (GNNs)**: For modeling knowledge structure relationships
- **Multi-modal learning**: Combining text, video, and interaction data
- **Temporal modeling**: Capturing learning progression over time
- **Federated learning**: Privacy-preserving distributed modeling

## 6. Intelligent Tutoring Systems (ITS)

### Core ITS Components
Modern ITS architectures include:
- **Domain model**: Representation of subject matter knowledge
- **Student model**: Current knowledge state and misconceptions
- **Tutoring model**: Pedagogical strategies and intervention rules
- **Interface module**: User interaction and feedback delivery

### Advanced ITS Research
**Ghosh et al. (2020)** [Context-Aware Attentive Knowledge Tracing](https://doi.org/10.1145/3394486.3403282) introduces AKT, which combines attention-based neural networks with interpretable components inspired by cognitive and psychometric models, achieving state-of-the-art performance while maintaining interpretability.

## 7. Large Language Models in Education

### Generative AI Applications
Recent advances in LLMs have transformed educational technology:

**Personalized Content Generation**:
- Adaptive exercise creation
- Explanatory text generation at appropriate reading levels
- Multimodal learning material synthesis

**Intelligent Tutoring**:
- Conversational tutoring agents
- Step-by-step problem solving guidance
- Socratic questioning generation

**Assessment & Feedback**:
- Automated essay scoring with detailed feedback
- Rubric-based evaluation
- Plagiarism detection with educational context

### Challenges & Opportunities
**Francis et al. (2025)** [Generative AI in Higher Education: Balancing Innovation and Integrity](https://doi.org/10.3389/bjbs.2024.14048) discusses the dual-edged nature of GenAI integration, highlighting both enhancement opportunities and academic integrity challenges.

## 8. Self-Regulated Learning & Human-AI Collaboration

### Hybrid Intelligence Approaches
**Molenaar (2022)** [Towards hybrid human-AI learning technologies](https://doi.org/10.1111/ejed.12527) introduces the augmentation perspective and hybrid intelligence concept for framing AI in education, emphasizing human-AI collaboration rather than replacement.

**Järvelä et al. (2023)** [Human and artificial intelligence collaboration for socially shared regulation in learning](https://doi.org/10.1111/bjet.13325) operationalizes human-AI collaboration for supporting socially shared regulation of learning, presenting an exciting prospect for advancing learning regulation support.

### Self-Regulation Support Systems
Modern adaptive systems incorporate:
- **Metacognitive prompting**: Encouraging reflection and planning
- **Goal-setting support**: Helping students set and track learning objectives
- **Progress monitoring**: Visualizing learning trajectories
- **Strategy recommendation**: Suggesting effective learning approaches

## 9. Key Datasets & Benchmarks

### Educational Data Mining Datasets
1. **ASSISTments**: Mathematics tutoring data with skill tags
2. **KDD Cup 2010**: Large-scale educational data mining challenge dataset
3. **EdNet**: Comprehensive dataset from Korean online education platform
4. **MOOCs datasets**: Coursera, edX, and Khan Academy interaction data
5. **Cognitive Tutor datasets**: Data from Carnegie Learning's math tutors

### Evaluation Metrics
- **AUC-ROC**: Area under ROC curve for binary prediction
- **RMSE**: Root mean squared error for continuous predictions
- **Accuracy**: Overall correct prediction rate
- **F1-score**: Balance of precision and recall
- **NDCG**: Normalized discounted cumulative gain for recommendation quality

## 10. Research Gaps & Future Directions

### Current Limitations
1. **Interpretability vs. Performance trade-off**: Deep models often lack transparency
2. **Data scarcity**: Limited labeled educational data for many domains
3. **Generalization**: Models often fail to transfer across domains or populations
4. **Ethical considerations**: Bias, fairness, and privacy concerns
5. **Integration challenges**: Difficulties deploying research models in production

### Emerging Research Areas
1. **Multimodal learning analytics**: Combining video, audio, and interaction data
2. **Explainable AI for education**: Making model decisions transparent to stakeholders
3. **Federated learning**: Privacy-preserving distributed model training
4. **Neuro-symbolic approaches**: Combining neural networks with symbolic reasoning
5. **Lifelong learning models**: Tracking knowledge across extended timeframes

## 11. Production Systems & Implementation Considerations

### Scalability Requirements
- **Real-time adaptation**: Sub-second response times for interactive systems
- **High concurrency**: Support for thousands of simultaneous users
- **Data persistence**: Long-term storage of learning trajectories
- **Interoperability**: Integration with existing educational systems (LMS, SIS)

### Deployment Challenges
- **Institutional adoption**: Overcoming organizational resistance
- **Teacher training**: Supporting educators in using adaptive systems
- **Infrastructure requirements**: Computational resources for model serving
- **Maintenance costs**: Ongoing model updating and system monitoring

## Conclusion

The field of adaptive learning systems has evolved significantly from early BKT and IRT models to sophisticated deep learning approaches and LLM-powered systems. Key trends include the integration of interpretable AI techniques, human-AI collaborative learning paradigms, and scalable cloud-based architectures. Future research should focus on addressing ethical concerns, improving model transparency, and developing robust evaluation frameworks that capture both learning outcomes and process quality.

## Agent 3: intelligent-tutoring-systems-foundations

Based on my comprehensive search, I can now provide you with a structured research overview of foundational intelligent tutoring systems. Let me organize the findings into a comprehensive report.

# Foundational Intelligent Tutoring Systems: A Comprehensive Research Landscape (2018-2026)

## Executive Summary

This research survey examines the evolution and current state of Intelligent Tutoring Systems (ITS), covering foundational architectures, modeling approaches, dialogue systems, domain modeling, student modeling, and modern AI/ML applications in education. The landscape spans from classical cognitive architectures to contemporary large language model applications.

## 1. ITS History and Foundational Architectures

### 1.1 ACT-R and Cognitive Tutor Systems

**John R. Anderson et al. (2007)** [Cognitive Tutor: Applied research in mathematics education](https://doi.org/10.3758/bf03194060). This foundational work established the Cognitive Tutor framework based on ACT-R cognitive architecture, demonstrating significant learning gains in mathematics education through model-tracing tutors.

**Albert T. Corbett et al. (2001)** [Cognitive Tutors: From the Research Classroom to All Classrooms](https://doi.org/10.4324/9781410601933-19). Describes the evolution of Cognitive Tutors from research prototypes to widely deployed educational systems, emphasizing the ACT-R cognitive architecture foundation.

### 1.2 AutoTutor and Dialogue-Based Systems

**Arthur C. Graesser et al. (2005)** [AutoTutor: An Intelligent Tutoring System With Mixed-Initiative Dialogue](https://doi.org/10.1109/te.2005.856149). Introduces AutoTutor as a conversational ITS that simulates human tutoring through natural language dialogue, achieving learning gains of approximately 0.8 sigma.

**Benjamin D. Nye et al. (2014)** [AutoTutor and Family: A Review of 17 Years of Natural Language Tutoring](https://doi.org/10.1007/s40593-014-0029-5). Comprehensive review of the AutoTutor family of systems, documenting 17 years of research and development in natural language tutoring.

### 1.3 ANDES and Constraint-Based Systems

**Antonija Mitrović (2011)** [Fifteen years of constraint-based tutors: what we have achieved and where we are going](https://doi.org/10.1007/s11257-011-9105-9). Reviews the development of constraint-based modeling approaches exemplified by ANDES, highlighting achievements and future directions in this paradigm.

## 2. Model Tracing vs. Constraint-Based Modeling Approaches

### 2.1 Theoretical Foundations

**Viswanathan Kodaganallur et al. (2006)** [An Assessment of Constraint-Based Tutors: A Response to Mitrovic and Ohlsson's Critique](https://doi.org/10.3233/irg-2006-16(3)06). Provides a detailed comparison of model-tracing and constraint-based paradigms, addressing theoretical debates between the approaches.

**Brent Martin (2002)** [Intelligent tutoring systems: The practical implementation of constraint-based modelling](http://hdl.handle.net/10092/4834). Examines practical implementation aspects of constraint-based modeling in ITS development.

### 2.2 Modern Implementations

**Vincent Aleven et al. (2016)** [Example-Tracing Tutors: Intelligent Tutor Development for Non-programmers](https://doi.org/10.1007/s40593-015-0088-2). Introduces example-tracing tutors as a more accessible approach to ITS development, bridging model-tracing and constraint-based approaches.

## 3. Dialogue-Based Tutoring: Conversational Strategies and Scaffolding

### 3.1 Natural Language Dialogue Systems

**José Paladines & Jaime Ramírez (2020)** [A Systematic Literature Review of Intelligent Tutoring Systems With Dialogue in Natural Language](https://doi.org/10.1109/access.2020.3021383). Comprehensive review of 33 ITSs incorporating natural language dialogue systems over 20 years.

**Arthur C. Graesser (2016)** [Conversations with AutoTutor Help Students Learn](https://doi.org/10.1007/s40593-015-0086-4). Demonstrates how conversational interactions in AutoTutor facilitate deeper learning through scaffolding and dialogue strategies.

### 3.2 Affective and Motivational Support

**Sidney K. D'Mello et al. (2007)** [Automatic detection of learner's affect from conversational cues](https://doi.org/10.1007/s11257-007-9037-6). Presents methods for detecting learner affect from conversational patterns in dialogue-based tutoring.

**Scotty D. Craig et al. (2004)** [Affect and learning: An exploratory look into the role of affect in learning with AutoTutor](https://doi.org/10.1080/1358165042000283101). Investigates relationships between affective states (frustration, boredom, flow, confusion) and learning outcomes in AutoTutor.

## 4. Domain Modeling: Expert Models, Bug Libraries, Misconception Catalogs

### 4.1 Knowledge Representation

**Kenneth R. Koedinger et al. (2012)** [The Knowledge-Learning-Instruction Framework: Bridging the Science-Practice Chasm](https://doi.org/10.1111/j.1551-6709.2012.01245.x). Introduces the KLI framework for systematic domain modeling and knowledge representation in ITS.

**Michel C. Desmarais & Ryan S. Baker (2011)** [A review of recent advances in learner and skill modeling in intelligent learning environments](https://doi.org/10.1007/s11257-011-9106-8). Reviews advances in domain modeling, including expert models and bug libraries for student misconception diagnosis.

### 4.2 Constraint-Based Domain Modeling

**Antonija Mitrović (2011)** [Fifteen years of constraint-based tutors: what we have achieved and where we are going](https://doi.org/10.1007/s11257-011-9105-9). Discusses constraint-based approaches to domain modeling, including bug libraries and misconception catalogs.

## 5. Student Modeling: Affect Detection, Engagement, Knowledge Estimation

### 5.1 Knowledge Tracing and Skill Modeling

**Ghodai Abdelrahman et al. (2022)** [Knowledge Tracing: A Survey](https://doi.org/10.1145/3569576). Comprehensive survey of knowledge tracing methods for tracking student knowledge states over time.

**Andrea Zanellati et al. (2024)** [Hybrid Models for Knowledge Tracing: A Systematic Literature Review](https://doi.org/10.1109/tlt.2023.3348690). Reviews hybrid approaches combining machine learning with cognitive models for knowledge tracing.

### 5.2 Affect Detection and Engagement

**Areej Alhothali (2011)** [Modeling User Affect Using Interaction Events](http://hdl.handle.net/10012/6027). Presents methods for affect detection using interaction patterns rather than intrusive sensors.

**Sidney K. D'Mello et al. (2011)** [A Motivationally Supportive Affect-Sensitive AutoTutor](https://doi.org/10.1007/978-1-4419-9625-1_9). Describes affect-sensitive tutoring systems that adapt to student motivational states.

## 6. Modern AI/ML Applications in ITS (2018-2026)

### 6.1 Large Language Models in Education

**Chung Kwan Lo (2023)** [What Is the Impact of ChatGPT on Education? A Rapid Review of the Literature](https://doi.org/10.3390/educsci13040410). Examines the transformative potential of ChatGPT and LLMs in educational settings.

**Aras Bozkurt et al. (2023)** [Speculative futures on ChatGPT and generative artificial intelligence (AI): A collective reflection from the educational landscape](https://doi.org/10.1111/bjet.13560). Explores potential futures of AI in education through speculative narratives.

### 6.2 Educational Chatbots and Conversational AI

**Mohammad Amin Kuhail et al. (2022)** [Interacting with educational chatbots: A systematic review](https://doi.org/10.1007/s10639-022-11177-3). Systematic review of 36 papers on educational chatbot interaction design and effectiveness.

**Aras Bozkurt (2023)** [Unleashing the Potential of Generative AI, Conversational Agents and Chatbots in Educational Praxis](https://doi.org/10.55982/openpraxis.15.4.609). Bibliometric analysis of generative AI applications in education.

### 6.3 AI-Driven Personalization

**Ivica Pesovski et al. (2024)** [Generative AI for Customizable Learning Experiences](https://doi.org/10.3390/su16073034). Presents approaches for personalized learning using generative AI within existing educational frameworks.

**Nam Ju Kim et al. (2022)** [Teacher's Perceptions of Using an Artificial Intelligence-Based Educational Tool for Scientific Writing](https://doi.org/10.3389/feduc.2022.755914). Investigates teacher perspectives on AI tools for personalized writing instruction.

## 7. Systematic Reviews and Meta-Analyses

### 7.1 ITS Effectiveness

**Lu Guo et al. (2021)** [Evolution and trends in intelligent tutoring systems research: a multidisciplinary and scientometric view](https://doi.org/10.1007/s12564-021-09697-7). Scientometric analysis of ITS research trends and evolution across disciplines.

**Ali Alkhatlan & Jugal Kalita (2019)** [Intelligent Tutoring Systems: A Comprehensive Historical Survey with Recent Developments](https://doi.org/10.5120/ijca2019918451). Comprehensive historical survey of ITS from foundational systems to modern developments.

### 7.2 Scaffolding and Problem-Based Learning

**Nam Ju Kim et al. (2017)** [Effectiveness of Computer-Based Scaffolding in the Context of Problem-Based Learning for Stem Education: Bayesian Meta-analysis](https://doi.org/10.1007/s10648-017-9419-1). Bayesian meta-analysis of computer-based scaffolding effectiveness in STEM education.

**Brian R. Belland (2016)** [Instructional Scaffolding in STEM Education](https://doi.org/10.1007/978-3-319-02565-0). Theoretical framework for instructional scaffolding in STEM contexts.

## 8. Future Directions and Challenges

### 8.1 Hybrid Intelligence and Human-AI Collaboration

**Sanna Järvelä et al. (2025)** [Hybrid intelligence: Human–AI coevolution and learning](https://doi.org/10.1111/bjet.13560). Explores human-AI coevolution in educational contexts and hybrid intelligence approaches.

**Jinhee Kim et al. (2022)** [Learning design to support student-AI collaboration: perspectives of leading teachers for AI in education](https://doi.org/10.1007/s10639-021-10831-6). Examines design principles for effective student-AI collaboration in learning environments.

### 8.2 Ethical and Implementation Challenges

**Melissa Bond et al. (2024)** [A meta systematic review of artificial intelligence in higher education: a call for increased ethics, collaboration, and rigour](https://doi.org/10.1186/s41239-023-00436-z). Meta-review highlighting ethical considerations and implementation challenges in AI education.

**Miriam Sullivan et al. (2023)** [ChatGPT in higher education: Considerations for academic integrity and student learning](https://doi.org/10.37074/jalt.2023.6.1.17). Addresses academic integrity concerns and pedagogical opportunities with generative AI.

## 9. Key Production Systems and Datasets

### 9.1 Production ITS Platforms
- **Cognitive Tutor Authoring Tools (CTAT)**: For creating example-tracing tutors
- **AutoTutor**: Natural language dialogue platform
- **ASSISTments**: Web-based mathematics tutoring platform
- **ALEKS**: Adaptive learning system for mathematics
- **Khan Academy**: Large-scale adaptive learning platform

### 9.2 Research Datasets
- **ASSISTments Dataset**: Student interaction data from mathematics tutoring
- **OULAD**: Open University Learning Analytics Dataset
- **EdNet**: Large-scale hierarchical dataset of student-system interactions
- **MOOCs datasets**: Various massive open online course interaction datasets

## 10. Methodological Trends

### 10.1 From Cognitive Models to Deep Learning
The field has evolved from rule-based cognitive models (ACT-R) to statistical approaches (Bayesian Knowledge Tracing) to modern deep learning methods (Transformer-based models).

### 10.2 Multimodal Learning Analytics
Increasing integration of multimodal data (text, speech, facial expressions, physiological signals) for comprehensive student modeling.

### 10.3 Explainable AI in Education
Growing emphasis on interpretable and explainable AI models to support teacher understanding and trust.

## Conclusion

The ITS field has evolved from foundational cognitive architectures to sophisticated AI-driven systems. Key trends include:
1. **Integration of LLMs** for natural language interaction and content generation
2. **Multimodal affect detection** for comprehensive student modeling
3. **Hybrid approaches** combining cognitive models with machine learning
4. **Scalable deployment** through cloud-based and mobile platforms
5. **Ethical frameworks** for responsible AI in education

The convergence of cognitive science, learning theory, and AI technologies continues to drive innovation in personalized, adaptive learning systems that can scale to meet diverse educational needs.

## Agent 4: learning-analytics-foundations

Based on my comprehensive search, I now have enough material to provide a structured analysis. Let me organize the findings into a comprehensive landscape of learning analytics and educational data mining research.

# Comprehensive Landscape of Learning Analytics and Educational Data Mining (2018-2026)

## Executive Summary

This research survey provides a comprehensive analysis of AI/ML applications in learning and studying across multiple domains. The landscape reveals significant advancements in educational data mining, learning analytics, adaptive learning systems, and the integration of large language models in education. Key trends include the shift toward personalized learning, ethical considerations in AI deployment, and the development of interpretable models for educational applications.

## 1. Foundational Educational Data Mining Techniques

### 1.1 Classification and Prediction Models
Recent research demonstrates sophisticated machine learning approaches for student performance prediction:

**Student Performance Prediction Using Machine Learning Algorithms** (Ahmed, 2024) presents a comprehensive framework using various ML algorithms to predict academic success, highlighting the importance of feature engineering and model selection in educational contexts.

**Advanced Deep Learning Model for Predicting Academic Performances** (Baniata et al., 2024) introduces deep learning architectures specifically designed for educational data, addressing challenges in handling heterogeneous student data sources.

### 1.2 Ensemble and Hybrid Approaches
**Predictive Models for Educational Purposes: A Systematic Review** (Almalawi et al., 2024) compares traditional statistical models with machine learning approaches, finding that ensemble methods and hybrid models show superior performance in educational prediction tasks.

### 1.3 Knowledge Tracing and Interpretability
**FDKT: Towards an Interpretable Deep Knowledge Tracing via Fuzzy Reasoning** (Liu et al., 2024) addresses the black-box nature of deep learning models in education by incorporating fuzzy reasoning for better interpretability while maintaining predictive accuracy.

## 2. Learning Management System (LMS) Data Analytics

### 2.1 xAPI and Data Standards
**Video Analytics in Moodle Using xAPI** (Judel et al., 2024) demonstrates the implementation of xAPI standards for tracking video interactions in Moodle, enabling comprehensive learning analytics across different content types.

**An Enhanced xAPI Data Model Supporting Assessment Analytics** (Nouira et al., 2018) extends xAPI specifications to better support assessment analytics, providing richer context for learning activity analysis.

### 2.2 Clickstream and Behavioral Analysis
**Analyzing click data with AI: implications for student performance prediction and learning assessment** (Borna et al., 2024) explores the use of clickstream data for predicting student performance, highlighting patterns in navigation behavior that correlate with learning outcomes.

**Analyzing Student Behavioral Patterns in MOOCs Using Hidden Markov Models** (Verykios et al., 2024) applies HMMs to MOOC log data to identify behavioral patterns and predict student engagement levels.

## 3. Early Warning Systems for At-Risk Students

### 3.1 Predictive Analytics for Dropout Prevention
**Dropout in online higher education: a systematic literature review** (Rahmani et al., 2024) synthesizes research on dropout prediction, identifying key predictors including engagement metrics, academic performance patterns, and demographic factors.

**Predicting Academic Success of College Students Using Machine Learning Techniques** (Guanin-Fajardo et al., 2024) applies CRISP-DM methodology to develop early warning systems that identify at-risk students during their first year of college.

### 3.2 Multi-Layer Personalized Approaches
**Multi-Layer Personalized Federated Learning for Mitigating Biases in Student Predictive Analytics** (Chu et al., 2022) addresses bias in predictive models by implementing federated learning approaches that account for different student subgroups and demographic characteristics.

## 4. Sequence Mining and Process Mining for Learning Paths

### 4.1 Temporal Analysis of Learning Processes
**Enhancing Personalized Learning Through Process Mining** (Wambsganß & Schmitt, 2024) applies process mining techniques to analyze learning pathways, identifying optimal sequences and detecting deviations from expected learning patterns.

**Enhancing academic performance prediction with temporal graph networks for massive open online courses** (Huang & Chen, 2024) incorporates temporal information and interaction behaviors into predictive models, improving accuracy by capturing the dynamic nature of learning.

## 5. Dashboards and Visualization for Learners and Instructors

### 5.1 Learning Analytics Dashboards
**Impact of Learning Analytics Guidance on Student Self-Regulated Learning Skills** (Tzimas & Demetriadis, 2024) evaluates the effectiveness of learning analytics dashboards in promoting self-regulated learning, finding significant improvements in student metacognitive skills.

**The effects of visualisation literacy and data storytelling dashboards on teachers' cognitive load** (Liu et al., 2024) examines how dashboard design affects teacher interpretation of analytics, emphasizing the importance of visualization literacy and data storytelling techniques.

### 5.2 Institutional Adoption Factors
**Adoption of learning analytics in higher education institutions: A systematic literature review** (Márquez et al., 2023) identifies key factors influencing institutional adoption, including organizational culture, technical infrastructure, and faculty training requirements.

## 6. AI/ML Applications Across Learning Domains

### 6.1 Large Language Models in Education
**Generative AI for Customizable Learning Experiences** (Pesovski et al., 2024) presents a framework for using generative AI to create personalized learning materials, demonstrating significant improvements in learning outcomes through adaptive content generation.

**AI and English language teaching: Affordances and challenges** (Crompton et al., 2024) systematically reviews LLM applications in language education, identifying specific affordances for language learning while addressing implementation challenges.

### 6.2 Intelligent Tutoring Systems
**Evaluating Recent Advances in Affective Intelligent Tutoring Systems** (Fernández-Herrero, 2024) reviews affective ITS that adapt to students' emotional states, showing improved learning outcomes through emotional regulation and personalized feedback.

**A comprehensive review of large language models: issues and solutions in learning environments** (Shahzad et al., 2025) analyzes challenges in deploying LLMs for educational purposes and proposes solutions for bias mitigation, content accuracy, and pedagogical alignment.

### 6.3 Adaptive Learning Systems
**Education 4.0 and 5.0: integrating Artificial Intelligence (AI) for personalized and adaptive learning** (Rane, 2024) explores the evolution of adaptive learning systems within Education 4.0 and 5.0 frameworks, highlighting the integration of AI for real-time personalization.

## 7. Ethical Considerations and Responsible AI

### 7.1 Bias and Fairness
**Could the Use of AI in Higher Education Hinder Students With Disabilities?** (Pierrès et al., 2024) examines potential negative impacts of AI systems on students with disabilities, advocating for inclusive design principles in educational AI development.

**The potential impact of Artificial Intelligence on equity and inclusion in education** (Varsik & Vosberg, 2024) analyzes how AI can both promote and hinder educational equity, providing recommendations for responsible AI implementation.

### 7.2 Trustworthy AI in Education
**Augmenting Deep Neural Networks with Symbolic Educational Knowledge** (Hooshyar et al., 2024) proposes hybrid approaches that combine neural networks with symbolic knowledge to create more trustworthy and interpretable educational AI systems.

## 8. Emerging Trends and Future Directions

### 8.1 Metaverse and Extended Reality Integration
**Learning Analytics and Educational Data Mining in Augmented Reality, Virtual Reality, and the Metaverse** (Evangelidis, 2025) explores the convergence of learning analytics with immersive technologies, identifying new opportunities for data collection and analysis in 3D learning environments.

### 8.2 Human-AI Collaborative Learning
**Artificial Intelligence in Educational Data Mining and Human-in-the-Loop Machine Learning** (López Menéses et al., 2025) examines human-AI collaboration frameworks, emphasizing the importance of teacher-in-the-loop approaches for effective educational AI deployment.

### 8.3 Sustainable Educational AI
**Advancing Sustainable Educational Practices Through AI-Driven Prediction of Academic Outcomes** (Albahli, 2025) connects AI applications with sustainability goals in education, demonstrating how predictive analytics can support resource optimization and equitable access.

## 9. Methodological Advances

### 9.1 Data Encoding and Representation
**Advancing Sustainable Learning Environments: A Literature Review on Data Encoding Techniques** (Ouahi et al., 2024) systematically reviews data preprocessing techniques for educational data, highlighting optimal approaches for different data types and learning contexts.

### 9.2 Federated Learning for Privacy Preservation
**Split Federated Learning for 6G Enabled-Networks** (Hafi et al., 2024) discusses federated learning approaches that enable collaborative model training while preserving student data privacy, particularly relevant for distributed educational systems.

## 10. Production Systems and Real-World Applications

### 10.1 Institutional Implementation
**Impact of Artificial Intelligence on Learning Management Systems: A Bibliometric Review** (Vergara et al., 2024) analyzes the integration of AI into commercial LMS platforms, identifying trends in feature development and adoption patterns.

### 10.2 Teacher Professional Development
**Teachers' AI digital competencies and twenty-first century skills in the post-pandemic world** (Ng et al., 2023) examines the skills required for effective AI integration in teaching, providing frameworks for teacher professional development in AI literacy.

## Key Findings and Implications

1. **Shift Toward Personalization**: There is a clear trend toward highly personalized learning experiences enabled by AI, with systems adapting to individual learning styles, paces, and preferences.

2. **Ethical Imperatives**: As AI becomes more integrated into education, ethical considerations around bias, privacy, and equity are receiving increased attention, driving research on responsible AI.

3. **Interpretability Requirements**: The need for interpretable AI models in education is driving research into explainable AI techniques and hybrid approaches that combine statistical and symbolic reasoning.

4. **Data Standardization**: The adoption of standards like xAPI and Caliper is facilitating more comprehensive learning analytics across different platforms and content types.

5. **Human-Centered Design**: Successful educational AI systems emphasize human-AI collaboration, with teachers maintaining central roles in instructional decision-making.

## Research Gaps and Future Directions

1. **Longitudinal Studies**: More research is needed on long-term impacts of AI-enhanced learning systems on student outcomes and development.

2. **Cross-Cultural Validity**: Most studies focus on specific educational contexts; research is needed on the cross-cultural applicability of educational AI systems.

3. **Integration Frameworks**: Comprehensive frameworks for integrating multiple AI technologies within cohesive educational ecosystems are still emerging.

4. **Assessment Innovation**: New approaches to assessment that leverage AI capabilities while maintaining validity and reliability require further development.

5. **Scalability Challenges**: Research on scaling successful pilot implementations to institutional and system-wide levels remains limited.

## Agent 5: llms-in-education-foundations

Based on my comprehensive search, I now have a substantial collection of papers covering all the domains you requested. Let me organize these findings into a structured report.

# Foundational Applications of LLMs in Education: A Comprehensive Research Landscape (2018-2026)

## Executive Summary

This research survey examines the foundational applications of Large Language Models (LLMs) in education across five key domains: (1) LLM-based tutoring systems, (2) prompt engineering for teaching, (3) conversational pedagogy, (4) content generation, and (5) risks and limitations. The analysis covers academic papers, methods, datasets, and production systems from 2018-2026, providing a comprehensive landscape of AI/ML applications for learning and studying.

## 1. LLM-Based Tutoring Systems

### 1.1 Foundational Research

**Bond et al. (2024)** [A meta systematic review of artificial intelligence in higher education: a call for increased ethics, collaboration, and rigour](https://doi.org/10.1186/s41239-023-00436-z). This highly cited meta-review (420 citations) analyzes AI applications in higher education, highlighting the evolution from traditional intelligent tutoring systems to LLM-powered approaches.

**Pesovski et al. (2024)** [Generative AI for Customizable Learning Experiences](https://doi.org/10.3390/su16073034). This influential paper (185 citations) presents an affordable approach to personalized learning using generative AI, demonstrating how LLMs enable truly customizable educational experiences.

**Ogunleye et al. (2024)** [A Systematic Review of Generative AI for Teaching and Learning Practice](https://doi.org/10.3390/educsci14060636). This systematic review (117 citations) provides comprehensive insights into GenAI applications in higher education, including tutoring systems.

### 1.2 Conversational Educational Agents

**Xi et al. (2026)** [Investigating the effects of an LLM-based Socratic conversational agent on students' academic performance and reflective thinking in higher education](https://doi.org/10.1016/j.compedu.2025.105494). This study examines Socratic dialogue implementation using LLM-based conversational agents.

**Córdova-Esparza (2025)** [AI-Powered Educational Agents: Opportunities, Innovations, and Ethical Challenges](https://doi.org/10.3390/info16060469). This systematic review of 82 studies analyzes technical and pedagogical frameworks for AI-powered educational agents.

**Modran et al. (2024)** [LLM Intelligent Agent Tutoring in Higher Education Courses using a RAG Approach](https://doi.org/10.20944/preprints202407.0519.v1). Proposes an innovative chatbot tutoring system integrating Retrieval Augmented Generation (RAG) for customized guidance.

## 2. Prompt Engineering for Teaching

### 2.1 Socratic Prompting and Scaffolded Dialogue

**Limongi (2026)** [Beyond Miracle Prompts: The Scholarly Prompting Framework for Prompt Engineering as Academic Competency](https://doi.org/10.2139/ssrn.6250940). Argues for treating prompt engineering as a multidimensional competency rather than just transferable recipes.

**Cain (2025)** [Prompting Learning: The EPICC 2 Framework for Effective Prompt Engineering in Education](https://doi.org/10.1201/9781003567257-2). Presents a framework specifically designed for educational prompt engineering.

**Yang & Zhu (2024)** [Heuristic question sequence generation based on retrieval augmentation](https://doi.org/10.46690/elder.2024.02.03). Applies AI to Socratic Method through personalized knowledge path planning algorithms.

### 2.2 Pedagogical Prompting Strategies

**Almeida (2025)** [Prompt Engineering: A Comparative Study of Prompting Techniques in AI Language Models](https://doi.org/10.1109/isec64801.2025.11147384). Comparative analysis of prompting techniques with educational applications.

**Developing (Foreign) Language Skills through Prompting/Prompt Writing/Prompt Engineering (2025)**. Focuses on language learning applications of prompt engineering.

## 3. Conversational Pedagogy

### 3.1 Turn-Taking and Dialogue Management

**Byeon et al. (2026)** [Understanding the Effects of Conversational Agent Personality on the Credibility of LLM-Based Conversational Search](https://doi.org/10.1145/3786304.3788843). Examines how agent personality affects credibility in educational conversations.

**SINGH et al. (2023)** [Catalyzing Python Learning: Assessing an LLM-based Conversational Agent](https://doi.org/10.58459/icce.2023.1478). Investigates interactions between students and conversational agents in programming education.

### 3.2 Error Correction and Explanation Generation

**Jury et al. (2024)** [Evaluating LLM-generated Worked Examples in an Introductory Programming Course](https://doi.org/10.1145/3636243.3636252). Examines LLM-generated worked examples with error correction capabilities (71 citations).

**Hao (2025)** [An LLM-Powered Grammatical Error Correction Agent with Explainable Feedback](https://doi.org/10.1145/3785987.3786075). Focuses on grammatical error correction with explainable feedback.

**Potter & Yuan (2024)** [LLM-based Code-Switched Text Generation for Grammatical Error Correction](https://doi.org/10.18653/v1/2024.emnlp-main.942). Applies LLMs to code-switched text generation for error correction.

## 4. Content Generation

### 4.1 Question Creation and Explanation Synthesis

**Gonzaga et al. (2026)** [CS Teaching Assistant Perceptions on LLM-Generated Faded Worked Examples for Feedback Training](https://doi.org/10.1145/3770762.3772582). Examines LLM-generated faded worked examples for computer science education.

**Xu et al. (2026)** [The Effects of Question Prompts and Worked Examples on Primary School Students' Scientific Achievement, Argumentation Skills, Motivation, and Cognitive Load](https://doi.org/10.3390/bs16030335). Studies question prompts and worked examples in scientific argumentation.

### 4.2 Worked Examples Generation

**Safadi & Ababsy (2020)** [Learning from troubleshooting activities when contrasting erroneous examples with worked examples in the physics classroom](https://doi.org/10.1088/1361-6552/ab9e1b). Foundational work on using erroneous vs. worked examples in physics education.

**Pillai et al. (2020)** [Are There Costs to Using Incorrect Worked Examples in Mathematics Education?](https://doi.org/10.31234/osf.io/tbwjk). Investigates potential drawbacks of incorrect worked examples.

## 5. Risks and Limitations

### 5.1 Hallucination in Education

**Cohen & Gerard (2026)** [Generative Artificial Intelligence (GenAI) and a Taxonomy of Undesirable Results](https://doi.org/10.2308/JETA-2024-045). Proposes a taxonomy for categorizing undesirable GenAI outputs, including hallucinations in educational contexts.

**Brodsky et al. (2025)** [Generative Artificial Intelligence in Anatomic Pathology](https://doi.org/10.5858/arpa.2024-0215-ra). While focused on medical education, provides insights into hallucination risks in specialized domains.

### 5.2 Over-Reliance and Equity Concerns

**Avraamidou (2024)** [Can we disrupt the momentum of the AI colonization of science education?](https://doi.org/10.1002/tea.21961). Critically examines over-reliance on AI and potential colonization of educational spaces.

**Zhao et al. (2026)** [Exploring the Design of GenAI-Based Systems to Support Socially Shared Metacognition](https://kclpure.kcl.ac.uk/portal/en/publications/e826473b-d273-4fdb-be8f-643c13f910de). Addresses over-reliance concerns in collaborative learning contexts.

**Hardy (2026)** [Autoscoring Anticlimax: A Meta-analytic Understanding of AI's Short-answer Shortcomings and Wording Weaknesses](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04820). Meta-analysis revealing limitations in AI-based assessment systems.

### 5.3 Equity and Bias Considerations

**Eden et al. (2024)** [Integrating AI in education: Opportunities, challenges, and ethical considerations](https://doi.org/10.30574/msarr.2024.10.2.0039). Comprehensive analysis of ethical challenges including equity concerns (137 citations).

**Bond et al. (2024)** [A meta systematic review of artificial intelligence in higher education: a call for increased ethics, collaboration, and rigour](https://doi.org/10.1186/s41239-023-00436-z). Emphasizes ethical considerations and equity in AI adoption.

## 6. Cognitive Science and Learning Foundations

### 6.1 Adaptive Learning Systems

**Demartini et al. (2024)** [Artificial Intelligence Bringing Improvements to Adaptive Learning in Education: A Case Study](https://doi.org/10.3390/su16031347). Examines AI improvements to adaptive learning systems (99 citations).

**Barrera Castro et al. (2024)** [Harnessing AI for Education 4.0: Drivers of Personalized Learning](https://doi.org/10.34190/ejel.22.5.3467). Systematic review identifying key drivers of personalized learning with AI (87 citations).

### 6.2 Self-Regulated Learning

**Hartley et al. (2024)** [Artificial Intelligence Supporting Independent Student Learning: An Evaluative Case Study of ChatGPT and Learning to Code](https://doi.org/10.3390/educsci14020120). Evaluates ChatGPT's support for self-regulated learning in programming (61 citations).

**Zhu et al. (2026)** [Scaffolding Metacognition with GenAI: Exploring Design Opportunities to Support Task Management for University Students with ADHD](http://arxiv.org/abs/2602.09381). Explores GenAI for scaffolding metacognition in students with ADHD.

### 6.3 Human-AI Collaborative Learning

**Järvelä et al. (2025)** [Hybrid intelligence: Human–AI coevolution and learning](https://doi.org/10.1111/bjet.13560). Examines human-AI coevolution in learning contexts (25 citations).

**Daryanto et al. (2025)** [Conversate: Supporting Reflective Learning in Interview Practice Through Interactive Simulation and Dialogic Feedback](https://doi.org/10.1145/3701188). Demonstrates human-AI collaboration in interview practice.

## 7. Assessment and Evaluation

### 7.1 Automated Assessment Systems

**Sun et al. (2024)** [Would ChatGPT-facilitated programming mode impact college students' programming behaviors, performances, and perceptions? An empirical study](https://doi.org/10.1186/s41239-024-00446-5). Empirical study on ChatGPT's impact on programming assessment (116 citations).

**Ng et al. (2023)** [Teachers' AI digital competencies and twenty-first century skills in the post-pandemic world](https://doi.org/10.1007/s11423-023-10203-6). Examines teacher competencies for AI-based assessment (497 citations).

### 7.2 Learning Analytics Integration

**Qushem et al. (2025)** [Technology-enhanced Learning and Learning Analytics for personalized STEM learning: A scoping review](https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ijer.2025.102827). Scoping review of learning analytics for personalized STEM learning.

**Ncube & Ngulube (2024)** [Optimising Data Analytics to Enhance Postgraduate Student Academic Achievement: A Systematic Review](https://doi.org/10.3390/educsci14111263). Systematic review of data analytics optimization for academic achievement.

## 8. Emerging Trends and Future Directions

### 8.1 Multi-Agent Systems

**Wang (2025)** [LLM-powered Multi-agent Framework for Goal-oriented Learning in Intelligent Tutoring System](https://doi.org/10.35542/osf.io/gt95h_v1). Proposes multi-agent framework for goal-oriented learning in ITS.

**Ben Hassouna et al. (2026)** [LLM-Agent-UMF: LLM-based Agent Unified Modeling Framework for Seamless Design of Multi Active/Passive Core-Agent Architectures](https://doi.org/10.1016/j.inffus.2025.103865). Presents unified modeling framework for multi-agent systems.

### 8.2 Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG)

**Modran et al. (2024)** [LLM Intelligent Agent Tutoring in Higher Education Courses using a RAG Approach](https://doi.org/10.20944/preprints202407.0519.v1). Demonstrates RAG approach for reducing hallucination in educational agents.

### 8.3 Ethical and Responsible AI

**Tan & Maravilla (2024)** [Shaping integrity: why generative artificial intelligence does not have to undermine education](https://doi.org/10.3389/frai.2024.1471224). Argues for responsible AI integration that maintains educational integrity (35 citations).

**Bozkurt et al. (2023)** [Speculative futures on ChatGPT and generative artificial intelligence (AI): A collective reflection from the educational landscape](https://eprints.gla.ac.uk/294292/1/294292.pdf). Collective reflection on ethical implications of GenAI in education (317 citations).

## 9. Methodological Approaches

### 9.1 Research Methods

- **Systematic Reviews**: Dominant approach for synthesizing evidence (Bond et al., 2024; Ogunleye et al., 2024)
- **Empirical Studies**: Increasing use of experimental designs (Sun et al., 2024; Jury et al., 2024)
- **Case Studies**: Common for examining implementation (Demartini et al., 2024; SINGH et al., 2023)
- **Bibliometric Analysis**: Growing for mapping research landscapes (Doğan & Şahin, 2024; Zhu et al., 2025)

### 9.2 Evaluation Metrics

- **Learning Outcomes**: Academic performance, skill acquisition
- **Engagement Metrics**: Interaction patterns, time on task
- **Quality Assessments**: Accuracy, relevance, pedagogical soundness
- **Ethical Considerations**: Bias detection, fairness metrics, privacy compliance

## 10. Key Challenges and Research Gaps

### 10.1 Technical Challenges
- Hallucination mitigation in educational contexts
- Scalability of personalized tutoring systems
- Integration with existing educational infrastructure
- Real-time adaptation to student needs

### 10.2 Pedagogical Challenges
- Balancing automation with human oversight
- Developing effective prompt engineering curricula
- Ensuring pedagogical soundness of AI-generated content
- Maintaining student agency and self-regulation

### 10.3 Ethical and Equity Challenges
- Addressing algorithmic bias in educational AI
- Ensuring equitable access to AI-powered tools
- Protecting student data privacy
- Preventing over-reliance and skill atrophy

## 11. Future Research Directions

1. **Longitudinal Studies**: Extended investigations of AI impact on learning trajectories
2. **Cross-Cultural Applications**: Adaptation of LLM-based systems across diverse educational contexts
3. **Integration Frameworks**: Development of standardized approaches for AI-education integration
4. **Teacher Training**: Research on effective professional development for AI literacy
5. **Policy Development**: Studies informing educational AI policy and governance

## 12. Conclusion

The landscape of LLM applications in education has evolved rapidly from 2018-2026, transitioning from theoretical exploration to practical implementation across multiple domains. While significant progress has been made in LLM-based tutoring, prompt engineering, conversational pedagogy, and content generation, substantial challenges remain regarding hallucination mitigation, over-reliance prevention, and equity assurance. The field requires continued interdisciplinary collaboration between AI researchers, educational scientists, cognitive psychologists, and ethicists to develop responsible, effective, and equitable AI-powered educational systems.

## Agent 6: assessment-evaluation-ai-foundations

Now let me compile all the findings into a comprehensive structured report:

# Foundational AI for Assessment and Evaluation: A Comprehensive Research Landscape (2018-2026)

## Executive Summary

This research survey provides a comprehensive landscape of AI/ML applications in educational assessment and evaluation, covering automated essay scoring, automated item generation, formative vs summative assessment with AI, fairness and bias considerations, computer-adaptive testing, and emerging trends with large language models. The analysis synthesizes findings from 50+ key papers published between 2018-2026, revealing significant advancements in neural approaches, ethical challenges, and practical implementations across educational domains.

## 1. Automated Essay Scoring (AES): Neural Approaches and Rubric Alignment

### 1.1 Evolution of AES Systems
**Dadi Ramesh and Suresh Kumar Sanampudi (2021)** [An automated essay scoring systems: a systematic literature review](https://doi.org/10.1007/s10462-021-10068-2) provides a comprehensive review of AES evolution, highlighting the transition from traditional feature-based approaches to deep learning methods. The review identifies key challenges in rubric alignment and cross-prompt generalization.

### 1.2 Neural Network Architectures
**Vive Kumar and David Boulanger (2020)** [Explainable Automated Essay Scoring: Deep Learning Really Has Pedagogical Value](https://doi.org/10.3389/feduc.2020.572367) demonstrates how deep learning models can provide rubric-level explanations, moving beyond holistic scoring to offer pedagogical insights. Their work emphasizes the importance of interpretability in AES systems.

### 1.3 Transformer-Based Approaches
**Elijah Mayfield and Alan W. Black (2020)** [Should You Fine-Tune BERT for Automated Essay Scoring?](https://doi.org/10.18653/v1/2020.bea-1.15) critically examines the cost-benefit analysis of fine-tuning large language models for AES, finding that BERT fine-tuning produces similar performance to classical models at significant additional computational cost.

### 1.4 Cross-Prompt Scoring
**Robert Ridley et al. (2021)** [Automated Cross-prompt Scoring of Essay Traits](https://doi.org/10.1609/aaai.v35i15.17620) addresses the challenge of generalizing across different writing prompts, developing methods for trait-specific scoring that maintain validity across diverse assessment contexts.

## 2. Automated Item Generation (AIG): Template-Based and Neural Methods

### 2.1 Systematic Review of AIG
**Ghader Kurdi et al. (2019)** [A Systematic Review of Automatic Question Generation for Educational Purposes](https://doi.org/10.1007/s40593-019-00186-y) analyzes 93 papers from 2015-2019, identifying trends in template-based approaches and emerging neural methods. The review highlights gaps in controlled difficulty generation and automated template construction.

### 2.2 Transformer-Based AIG
**Yigal Attali et al. (2022)** [The interactive reading task: Transformer-based automatic item generation](https://doi.org/10.3389/frai.2022.903077) introduces a novel approach using transformer models for generating reading comprehension items, demonstrating improved construct alignment and item quality.

### 2.3 Construct-Specific Generation
**Björn Erik Hommel et al. (2021)** [Transformer-Based Deep Neural Language Modeling for Construct-Specific Automatic Item Generation](https://doi.org/10.1007/s11336-021-09823-9) applies transformer models to generate items for non-cognitive constructs, addressing limitations of traditional template-based approaches in personality and attitude assessment.

### 2.4 LLM-Based Item Generation
**Ayfer Sayin and Mark J. Gierl (2024)** [Using OpenAI GPT to Generate Reading Comprehension Items](https://doi.org/10.1111/emip.12590) explores the use of GPT models for generating reading comprehension items, demonstrating both opportunities and challenges in maintaining psychometric quality.

## 3. Formative vs Summative Assessment with AI

### 3.1 AI in Educational Assessment Landscape
**J. Gardner et al. (2021)** [Artificial intelligence in educational assessment: 'Breakthrough? Or buncombe and ballyhoo?'](https://doi.org/10.1111/jcal.12577) provides a critical analysis of AI applications in both formative and summative assessment contexts, examining automated essay scoring and computerized adaptive testing.

### 3.2 Formative Feedback Systems
**Clayton Cohn et al. (2024)** [A Chain-of-Thought Prompting Approach with LLMs for Evaluating Students' Formative Assessment Responses in Science](https://doi.org/10.1609/aaai.v38i21.30364) demonstrates how LLMs can provide detailed formative feedback using chain-of-thought reasoning, supporting K-12 science education.

### 3.3 Automated Short-Answer Grading
**Fetty Fitriyanti Lubis et al. (2021)** [Automated Short-Answer Grading using Semantic Similarity based on Word Embedding](https://doi.org/10.14716/ijtech.v12i3.4651) develops ASAG systems for formative assessment, using semantic similarity approaches to evaluate short-answer responses.

## 4. Fairness and Bias in AI-Based Assessment

### 4.1 Ethical Challenges in AI Assessment
**Okan Bulut and Maggie Beiting-Parrish (2024)** [The Rise of Artificial Intelligence in Educational Measurement: Opportunities and Ethical Challenges](https://doi.org/10.59863/miql7785) comprehensively examines ethical concerns including validity, reliability, transparency, and fairness in AI-based assessment systems.

### 4.2 Differential Item Functioning (DIF)
**Rudolf Debelak and Dries Debeer (2021)** [An Evaluation of DIF Tests in Multistage Tests for Continuous Covariates](https://doi.org/10.3390/psych3040040) investigates DIF detection methods in adaptive testing contexts, highlighting challenges in identifying bias with continuous covariates.

### 4.3 Fairness in Performance Prediction
**Marco Lünich et al. (2023)** [Fairness of Academic Performance Prediction for the Distribution of Support Measures for Students: Differences in Perceived Fairness of Distributive Justice Norms](https://doi.org/10.1007/s10758-023-09698-y) examines how AI-based performance predictions impact fairness perceptions in educational support allocation.

### 4.4 Trustworthy ML Framework
**Alex Gittens et al. (2022)** [An Adversarial Perspective on Accuracy, Robustness, Fairness, and Privacy: Multilateral-Tradeoffs in Trustworthy ML](https://doi.org/10.1109/access.2022.3218715) presents a framework for balancing competing objectives in trustworthy machine learning systems for assessment.

## 5. Computer-Adaptive Testing (CAT) Algorithms and Modern Extensions

### 5.1 Evidence-Centered Design
**Robert J. Mislevy et al. (2003)** [A BRIEF INTRODUCTION TO EVIDENCE‐CENTERED DESIGN](https://doi.org/10.1002/j.2333-8504.2003.tb01908.x) provides foundational principles for designing adaptive assessments, emphasizing the importance of evidentiary reasoning in item selection.

### 5.2 Modern CAT Applications
**Robert D. Gibbons et al. (2015)** [Computerized Adaptive Diagnosis and Testing of Mental Health Disorders](https://doi.org/10.1146/annurev-clinpsy-021815-093634) demonstrates advanced CAT applications in clinical assessment, using multidimensional item response theory and random forests.

### 5.3 Machine Learning Integration
**Adrienne Kline and Joon Lee (2023)** [Machine Learning Capability: A standardized metric using case difficulty with applications to individualized deployment of supervised machine learning](https://arxiv.org/abs/2302.04386) explores the integration of IRT and CAT with machine learning for benchmarking classification performance.

### 5.4 Parallel Test Assembly
**Luc Zimny et al. (2024)** [Ant colony optimization for parallel test assembly](https://doi.org/10.3758/s13428-023-02319-7) introduces optimization algorithms for assembling parallel test forms in adaptive testing contexts.

## 6. Large Language Models in Educational Assessment

### 6.1 Systematic Review of LLMs in Education
**Lixiang Yan et al. (2023)** [Practical and ethical challenges of large language models in education: A systematic scoping review](https://doi.org/10.1111/bjet.13370) analyzes 118 papers to identify 53 use cases for LLMs in educational tasks, categorizing them into nine main categories including grading, feedback, and content generation.

### 6.2 ChatGPT and Academic Integrity
**Jürgen Rudolph et al. (2023)** [ChatGPT: Bullshit spewer or the end of traditional assessments in higher education?](https://doi.org/10.37074/jalt.2023.6.1.9) examines the implications of ChatGPT for assessment design and academic integrity in higher education.

### 6.3 LLM-Based Essay Scoring
**Kevin Yancey et al. (2023)** [Rating Short L2 Essays on the CEFR Scale with GPT-4](https://doi.org/10.18653/v1/2023.bea-1.49) evaluates GPT-4's performance in scoring second-language essays, comparing results with human raters and traditional AES systems.

### 6.4 Generative AI in Assessment Design
**David Ernesto Salinas-Navarro et al. (2024)** [Using Generative Artificial Intelligence Tools to Explain and Enhance Experiential Learning for Authentic Assessment](https://doi.org/10.3390/educsci14010083) explores how generative AI can support authentic assessment design in experiential learning contexts.

## 7. Intelligent Tutoring Systems and Learning Analytics

### 7.1 Proactive and Reactive AI Engagement
**Sruti Mallik and Ahana Gangopadhyay (2023)** [Proactive and reactive engagement of artificial intelligence methods for education: a review](https://doi.org/10.3389/frai.2023.1151391) examines AI applications in intelligent tutoring and learning analytics, distinguishing between proactive and reactive system designs.

### 7.2 Trustworthy Peer Assessment
**Ali Darvishi et al. (2022)** [Incorporating AI and learning analytics to build trustworthy peer assessment systems](https://doi.org/10.1111/bjet.13233) develops AI-enhanced peer assessment systems that address concerns about feedback quality and grading accuracy.

### 7.3 Epistemological Foundations
**Simon Knight et al. (2014)** [Epistemology, Assessment, Pedagogy: Where Learning Meets Analytics in the Middle Space](https://doi.org/10.18608/jla.2014.12.3) provides theoretical foundations for learning analytics, emphasizing the interplay between epistemology, assessment, and pedagogy.

## 8. Key Datasets and Production Systems

### 8.1 Major AES Datasets
- **ASAP Dataset**: Widely used for automated essay scoring research
- **TOEFL/Cambridge English**: Large-scale language assessment datasets
- **Common Core State Standards**: Educational assessment datasets

### 8.2 Production Systems
- **ETS e-rater**: Commercial AES system with extensive validation
- **Pearson's Intelligent Essay Assessor**: Industry-standard AES platform
- **Turnitin's Revision Assistant**: Formative writing assessment tool
- **ALEKS**: Adaptive learning and assessment platform

### 8.3 Open-Source Tools
- **BERT-based AES implementations**: Various open-source models
- **Rasch analysis packages**: Psychometric analysis tools
- **CAT simulation frameworks**: Adaptive testing development tools

## 9. Research Gaps and Future Directions

### 9.1 Critical Research Needs
1. **Explainability and Transparency**: Developing interpretable AI models for high-stakes assessment
2. **Cross-Cultural Validity**: Ensuring fairness across diverse linguistic and cultural contexts
3. **Longitudinal Assessment**: Tracking learning progression with AI-enhanced methods
4. **Human-AI Collaboration**: Optimizing hybrid assessment systems
5. **Regulatory Frameworks**: Establishing standards for AI-based assessment validation

### 9.2 Emerging Trends
- **Multimodal Assessment**: Integrating text, speech, and behavioral data
- **Federated Learning**: Privacy-preserving assessment models
- **Quantum Machine Learning**: Potential applications in complex assessment tasks
- **Neuro-symbolic AI**: Combining neural and symbolic reasoning for assessment

## 10. Methodological Considerations

### 10.1 Validation Frameworks
- **Evidence-Centered Design (ECD)**: Systematic assessment design approach
- **Unified Validity Framework**: Comprehensive validation of AI assessment systems
- **Fairness Auditing**: Regular bias detection and mitigation procedures

### 10.2 Evaluation Metrics
- **Psychometric Properties**: Reliability, validity, and fairness metrics
- **Computational Efficiency**: Resource requirements and scalability
- **Human-AI Agreement**: Concordance with expert human judgment

## Conclusion

The landscape of AI in educational assessment has evolved significantly from 2018-2026, with neural approaches and large language models transforming traditional assessment paradigms. While substantial progress has been made in automated scoring, item generation, and adaptive testing, critical challenges remain in ensuring fairness, transparency, and validity. Future research must prioritize ethical considerations, human-centered design, and robust validation frameworks to realize the full potential of AI in enhancing educational assessment while maintaining trust and equity.
